urlpatterns approach. The main files implementing URL routing are:\\n\\n**Core URL Routing Module (django/urls/):**\\n- django/urls/__init__.py: Module initialization exporting the public API\\n- django/urls/base.py: Contains resolve() and reverse() functions that are the primary entry points for URL resolution and reversal. Also includes reverse_lazy() for lazy URL reversal, urlconf management (get_urlconf, set_urlconf), and URL validation (is_valid_path). These functions use the URLResolver to process URL patterns.\\n- django/urls/conf.py: Defines include() for including nested URL patterns, and path()/re_path() functions which are partial applications of _path(). These functions replace the old url() and patterns() from pre-1.10.\\n- django/urls/resolvers.py: The URL dispatcher core with URLResolver class that implements the resolve() method to match URLs against patterns. Contains URLPattern for endpoint patterns and URLResolver for nested URL patterns. Also includes ResolverMatch class representing a successful URL match. Pattern classes (RegexPattern, RoutePattern, LocalePrefixPattern) handle URL matching. The _populate() method builds reverse lookup dictionaries. Helper functions get_resolver() and get_ns_resolver() provide cached resolver instances.\\n- django/urls/converters.py: Path parameter converters (IntConverter, StringConverter, SlugConverter, PathConverter, UUIDConverter) used with the new path() syntax. register_converter() allows custom converters.\\n- django/urls/exceptions.py: Resolver404 and NoReverseMatch exceptions for URL resolution failures.\\n- django/urls/utils.py: Utility functions get_callable() for dynamic view importing and get_mod_func() for splitting module paths.\\n\\n**Configuration Module (django/conf/urls/):**\\n- django/conf/urls/__init__.py: Imports include() and exports error handlers (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500)\\n- django/conf/urls/i18n.py: i18n_patterns() function for language-prefixed URLs using LocalePrefixPattern, replacing the old i18n_patterns() wrapper from earlier versions.\\n- django/conf/urls/static.py: static() helper function for serving media files in development using re_path().\\n\\n**URL Validation (django/core/checks/urls.py):**\\n- Provides URL configuration validation including check_url_config(), check_resolver() which recursively validates URLPattern and URLResolver objects, check_url_namespaces_unique() to ensure namespace uniqueness, and get_warning_for_invalid_pattern() which warns about tuple patterns (legacy format from before path()/re_path()).\\n\\nThe migration from patterns() to the current system: The legacy patterns() function returned a tuple of URL patterns for use with url(). The current system uses include() which returns a 3-tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace) handled by _path(). The URLResolver's resolve() method iterates through url_patterns (which are URLPattern or URLResolver objects) and matches them against the path. Django URL routing system has evolved from the legacy patterns() function (pre-1.10) to the current list-based urlpatterns approach. The main files implementing URL routing are:\\n\\n**Core URL Routing Module (django/urls/):**\\n- django/urls/__init__.py: Module initialization exporting the public API\\n- django/urls/base.py: Contains resolve() and reverse() functions that are the primary entry points for URL resolution and reversal. Also includes reverse_lazy() for lazy URL reversal, urlconf management (get_urlconf, set_urlconf), and URL validation (is_valid_path). These functions use the URLResolver to process URL patterns.\\n- django/urls/conf.py: Defines include() for including nested URL patterns, and path()/re_path() functions which are partial applications of _path(). The _path() function creates URLPattern or URLResolver objects based on whether the view is a callable or a list/tuple (from include()). These functions replace the old url() and patterns() from pre-1.10.\\n- django/urls/resolvers.py: The URL dispatcher core with URLResolver class that implements the resolve() method to match URLs against patterns. Contains URLPattern for endpoint patterns and URLResolver for nested URL patterns. Also includes ResolverMatch class representing a successful URL match. Pattern classes (RegexPattern, RoutePattern, LocalePrefixPattern) handle URL matching. The _populate() method builds reverse lookup dictionaries. Helper functions get_resolver() and get_ns_resolver() provide cached resolver instances.\\n- django/urls/converters.py: Path parameter converters (IntConverter, StringConverter, SlugConverter, PathConverter, UUIDConverter) used with the new path() syntax. register_converter() allows custom converters.\\n- django/urls/exceptions.py: Resolver404 and NoReverseMatch exceptions for URL resolution failures.\\n- django/urls/utils.py: Utility functions get_callable() for dynamic view importing and get_mod_func() for splitting module paths.\\n\\n**Configuration Module (django/conf/urls/):**\\n- django/conf/urls/__init__.py: Imports include() and exports error handlers (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500)\\n- django/conf/urls/i18n.py: i18n_patterns() function for language-prefixed URLs using LocalePrefixPattern, replacing the old i18n_patterns() wrapper from earlier versions.\\n- django/conf/urls/static.py: static() helper function for serving media files in development using re_path().\\n\\n**URL Validation (django/core/checks/urls.py):**\\n- Provides URL configuration validation including check_url_config(), check_resolver() which recursively validates URLPattern and URLResolver objects, check_url_namespaces_unique() to ensure namespace uniqueness, and get_warning_for_invalid_pattern() which warns about tuple patterns (legacy format from before path()/re_path()).\\n\\nThe migration from patterns() to the current system: The legacy patterns() function returned a tuple of URL patterns for use with url(). The current system uses include() which returns a 3-tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace) handled by _path(). The URLResolver's resolve() method iterates through url_patterns (which are URLPattern or URLResolver objects) and matches them against the path. The reverse lookup uses _populate() to build dictionaries mapping view names to URL patterns for URL reversal with reverse().\"\n   238→}\n   239→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
